### Post by coffeecat on 2014-08-11
What is "Ogle"? A google search suggests that it might be a DVD player for Linux. If so, you're going about this entirely the wrong way. A default Ubuntu installation includes software that can play DVDs, and it requires only a couple of things to be installed (easily) to make it capable of playing commercial encrypted DVDs.

Because you are making common newbie mistakes from your conditioning with Windows, a couple of points:

1 - >95% of the software that you will ever need can be installed from the repositories via the Software Centre. Far easier than in Windows or in MacOS. You don't have to go trawling around the net and risk downloading software riddled with malware. **Don't** go hunting around the internet for software unless there is absolutely no other alternative. 

2 - If you need help finding software for a particular task, or configuring software already installed, please ask here.

---

### Post by nerdtron on 2014-08-11
My eyes hurt for reading your post. You may think that downloading/installing software in Ubuntu is the same as inn windows. You go to a website, download the installer and then run it.

Ubuntu works in a different way. This is a different operating system and it does this differently.
You see, you can just open the Ubuntu Software Center and then search for the software you like, then click Install. No more internet searching. If you want to install software not in the Software Center, that's a different story and will need manual download/install which can get a little complicated.

---

### Post by newb85 on 2014-08-11
Coffeecat is right on the money.  The place to start looking for software is the Software Center, which is much easier (and much safer) than the "Windows way" of downloading an executable installer through your browser from a random website you find with a Google search.

Using a laptop would seem complicated to someone who thought it should work like a typewriter.

### Post by coffeecat on 2014-08-11
Let's make sure you have everything installed that VLC and Videos need for full functionality. You may need extra codecs for Videos and libdvdcss2 for both if the DVDs are encrypted. These things can't be included in a default install of Ubuntu because of licensing restrictions.

Open Software Centre and search for ubuntu-restricted-extras. Install it. That will give you various audio and video codecs as well as other useful stuff such as the flash plugin for your browser. It also includes the Microsoft core fonts, so you need to monitor the installation process - you will be prompted to agree to a EULA for the core fonts. It's a formality - OK it, and the fonts on many websites will look better and you will have such things as Times New Roman and Arial available on your system.

For the next bit, you need to open a terminal - ctrl-alt-T is the shortcut. Run this command:

```
sudo /usr/share/doc/libdvdread4/install-css.sh
```

You will be prompted for your password but it will not be echoed to the screen. Simply type it in and press enter. That will install the library for the content scramble system.

If you find after this that both VLC and Videos do not have the functionality you want, try installing smplayer from the Software Centre. It's a fairly good video player, but I don't know how good it is with interactive DVDs.

As far as Ogle is concerned, the page you linked is dated 2008 which is prehistoric in Ubuntu terms, so even if the download link was valid the package wouldn't work in the latest version of Ubuntu. I don't know whether Ogle is still maintained and updated.

---

### Post by grahammechanical on 2014-08-11
Linux is not controlled by one massive commercial organization. Linux is open source and also open standards. This gives people a great freedom but that also brings a greater complexity. The Ubuntu developers have worked to make the Ubuntu distribution of Linux less complex for ordinary users.

Some developers will provide software that needs to be compiled once it has been downloaded. It has to be converted into a executable program. Some developers provide their software packaged for installation by a package installer. There are two package formats. Ubuntu is based upon Debian Linux and Debian has its deb format. Other Linux distributions are based upon Red Hat Linux and that uses the Red Hat Package Management (rpm) package format. The two package formats are not compatible.

Remember, this freedom is why we are able to download, install and use Linux distributions like Ubuntu without charge.

When I search for ogle in the software centre it informs me that I already have libdvdnav installed. That library is described as 

> a DVD navigation library, which provides an interface to the advanced features of DVDs, like menus and navigation. It contains the VM and other parts useful for writing DVD players. It is based on Ogle, but was modified to be used by xine and mplayer.

Regards.

### Post by nerdtron on 2014-08-12

### Post by amanchesterman on 2014-08-12
Can you list the content of the 'slides' section of the DVD using your file manager? I think in Ubuntu your file manager is Nautilus; I use Xubuntu, where it's a different app.
You would need to navigate to that part of the DVD by looking in the left hand pane of the file manager. Someone here who uses Nautilus can tell you how.
The point is that if you can see the files listed, you may be able to see what *type of file* the slides are. (You can probably right-click on one of them and see the 'file properties', that's how I do it on my machine.)
If, as I suspect, the slides are PowerPoint files they will have a .ppt or .pptx file extension. You will need to view them in a program that can display PowerPoint presentations. If you haven't got one installed already, you should find that the Libre Office package (available in the Software Center) can do it.

---

oh, and i just re-read your response.... yeah, they are definitely not slides in the powerpoint sense. they are video/audio clips like the rest of the DVD. somewhere.
